  <script type="text/javascript">
    (function() {
        var contextPath = '/jira';
        var eventBuffer = [];

        function printDeprecatedMsg() {
            if (console && console.warn) {
                console.warn('DEPRECATED JS - contextPath global variable has been deprecated since 7.4.0. Use `wrm/context-path` module instead.');
            }
        }

        function sendEvent(analytics, postfix) {
            analytics.send({
                name: 'js.globals.contextPath.' + postfix
            });
        }

        function sendDeprecatedEvent(postfix) {
            try {
                var analytics = require('jira/analytics');
                if (eventBuffer.length) {
                    eventBuffer.forEach(function(value) {
                        sendEvent(analytics, value);
                    });
                    eventBuffer = [];
                }

                if (postfix) {
                    sendEvent(analytics, postfix);
                }
            } catch(ex) {
                eventBuffer.push(postfix);
                setTimeout(sendDeprecatedEvent, 1000);
            }
        }

        Object.defineProperty(window, 'contextPath', {
            get: function() {
                printDeprecatedMsg();
                sendDeprecatedEvent('get');
                return contextPath;
            },
            set: function(value) {
                printDeprecatedMsg();
                sendDeprecatedEvent('set');
                contextPath = value;
            }
        });
    })();

</script>

\u003cdiv class=\\\"action-body flooded\\\"\u003e\u003cp\u003eHi Tomohito,\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eThe BatchUpdateException indicates that the error happens when executeBatch() is invoked, not when setXXX() or addBatch() is called. I think this is OK, but it would of course be better if the exception were raised in setXXX().\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eIf you want to ignore these errors in parameterMapping.java, you could wrap each call to executeBatch() like this:\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003etry {\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n    psi.executeBatch();\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n} catch (BatchUpdateException bue) {\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n    SQLException reason = bue.getNextException();\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n    throw (reason == null) ? bue : reason;\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n}\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eAlso, do you think a release note is needed for this issue? Hatlen\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n added a comment  - \u003cspan class=\'commentdate_12429278_verbose subText\'\u003e\u003cspan class=\'date user-tz\' title=\'20\\/Aug\\/06 17:40\'\u003e\u003ctime class=\'livestamp\' datetime=\'2006-08-20T17:40:35+0000\'\u003e20\\/Aug\\/06 17:40\u003c\\/time\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e  \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-body flooded\\\"\u003e\u003cp\u003eWith the \u003ca href=\\\"https:\\/\\/issues.apache.org\\/jira\\/browse\\/DERBY-1610\\\" title=\\\"Resolve difference of type compatibility between Embedded and NetworkServer\\/NetworkDriver\\\" class=\\\"issue-link\\\" data-issue-key=\\\"DERBY-1610\\\"\u003e\u003cdel\u003eDERBY-1610\u003c\\/del\u003e\u003c\\/a\u003e_2.diff patch, setBinaryStream(null), setBlob(null) and setNull(Types.BLOB) throw exception if they are called on a parameter of type CHAR, VARCHAR, LONGVARCHAR or CLOB. However, they can still be used to set parameters of other types (for instance SHORT, INTEGER, FLOAT, DOUBLE and TIMESTAMP) to null. I think it would be better and more consistent behaviour if all of these failed as well.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eIn fact, all other setXXX methods can be used to set null values on parameters of all types. I find it a bit unintuitive that only the combinations mentioned above should raise exceptions. However, they can still be used to set parameters of other types (for instance SHORT, INTEGER, FLOAT, DOUBLE and TIMESTAMP) to null. I think it would be better and more consistent behaviour if all of these failed as well. \\n\\n In fact, all other setXXX methods can be used to set null values on parameters of all types. \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-body flooded\\\"\u003e\u003cp\u003eThere will be user impact even if only a few of the incompatible combinations are changed to throw exceptions. Therefore, I think that it is better to fix all of them at once. Fixing only a couple of them makes the current state of the code harder to understand. For instance, I don\'t understand why setBlob(null) should fail on a CHAR parameter, but succeed on a DOUBLE parameter.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eAlso, I\'m not sure whether this type checking should happen on the server. Since the DRDA protocol doesn\'t preserve which JDBC method was used, and which arguments the user passed in, it might not always have enough information to decide what to do. Another problem with having the check on the server, is that old clients (or jcc clients) running against a new server will also get these new exceptions. Some people might call that a regression.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eIf it is possible to get the type checks on the client instead of on the server, I would prefer that solution. If that is not possible, I think we should only make sure that all setXXX(null) calls work as before \u003ca href=\\\"https:\\/\\/issues.apache.org\\/jira\\/browse\\/DERBY-1535\\\" title=\\\"Trial 2 for DERBY-550, improve use of Engine from NetworkServer and reduce memory usage\\\" class=\\\"issue-link\\\" data-issue-key=\\\"DERBY-1535\\\"\u003e\u003cdel\u003eDERBY-1535\u003c\\/del\u003e\u003c\\/a\u003e, and delay the change of behaviour until we have found a way to make all calls behave correctly.\u003c\\/p\u003e \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003cdiv class=\\\"twixi-wrap concise actionContainer\\\"\u003e\\n        \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-head\\\"\u003e\\n            \u003ca href=\\\"#\\\" title=\\\"Expand comment\\\" class=\\\"twixi\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"icon-default aui-icon aui-icon-small aui-iconfont-collapsed\\\"\u003e\u003cspan\u003eShow\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n            \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-details flooded\\\"\u003e\\n                        \\n    \\n    \\n    \\n                \\n\\n    \u003ca class=\\\"user-hover user-avatar\\\" rel=\\\"knutanders\\\" id=\\\"commentauthor_12429368_concise\\\" href=\\\"\\/jira\\/secure\\/ViewProfile.jspa?name=knutanders\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar aui-avatar-xsmall\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar-inner\\\"\u003e\u003cimg src=\\\"https:\\/\\/issues.apache.org\\/jira\\/secure\\/useravatar?size=xsmall&amp;avatarId=10452\\\" alt=\\\"knutanders\\\" \\/\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e Knut Anders Hatlen\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n added a comment  - \u003cspan class=\'commentdate_12429368_concise subText\'\u003e\u003cspan class=\'date user-tz\' title=\'21\\/Aug\\/06 09:34\'\u003e\u003ctime class=\'livestamp\' datetime=\'2006-08-21T09:34:29+0000\'\u003e21\\/Aug\\/06 09:34\u003c\\/time\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e                    There will be user impact even if only a few of the incompatible combinations are changed to throw exceptions. Therefore, I think that it is better to fix all of them at once. Fixing only a couple of them makes the current state of the code harder to understand. For instance, I don\'t understand why setBlob(null) should fail on a CHAR parameter, but succeed on a DOUBLE parameter. \\n\\n Also, I\'m not sure whether this type checking should happen on the server. Since the DRDA protocol doesn\'t preserve which JDBC method was used, and which arguments the user passed in, it might not always have enough information to decide what to do. Another problem with having the check on the server, is that old clients (or jcc clients) running against a new server will also get these new exceptions. Some people might call that a regression. \\n\\n If it is possible to get the type checks on the client instead of on the server, I would prefer that solution. If that is not possible, I think we should only make sure that all setXXX(null) calls work as before   DERBY-1535  , and delay the change of behaviour until we have found a way to make all calls behave correctly.              \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n\u003c\\/div\u003e\\n                             \\n\\n\\n\u003cdiv \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-body flooded\\\"\u003e\u003cp\u003eAlthough embedded throws XCL12 in some cases, I don\'t think the client driver needs to do the same. Change\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nIn a number of situations, Derby\'s client implementation behaved differently from the Embedded implementation:\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n1. setNull(LONGVARCHAR) on parameter of type CHAR FOR BIT DATA (Types.BINARY).\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n\\tIn previous releases, the Client succeeds, embedded fails (state 22005).\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n2. setNull(LONGVARBINARY) on parameter of type CHAR FOR BIT DATA (Types.BINARY).\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n\\tIn previous releases, Embedded succeeds, client fails (state 22005).\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n3. setNull(LONGVARBINARY) on parameter of type VARCHAR FOR BIT DATA (Types.VARBINARY).\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n\\tIn previous releases, Embedded succeeds, client fails (state 22005).\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n4. setNull(BINARY) on parameter of type LONG VARCHAR FOR BIT DATA (Types.LONGVARBINARY)\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n\\tIn previous releases, Embedded succeeds, client fails (state 22005).\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n5. setNull(TIME) on parameter of TIMESTAMP. \u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n\\tIn previous releases, Client succeeds, embedded fails (state 22005).\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eIncompatibilities with Previous Release\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nNow, in the cases indicated above, the client and Embedded implementation show the behavior previously shown only with Embedded.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eRationale for Change\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nDerby\'s Client implementation and Embedded implementation should behave the same way from the point of view of an application whenever possible.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eApplication Changes Required\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nApplications relying on the Client behaving in the old way will have to be adjusted.\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n------------------------------\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eIf class=\'livestamp\' datetime=\'2007-05-26T22:16:49+0000\'\u003e26\\/May\\/07 22:16\u003c\\/time\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e                    Hi, \\n\\n This issue is one of several that is in progress, however, if I understand it correctly, a change that might impact existing applications has already gone in, and will be in for 10.3. \\n\\n I too find it important to document this change in behavior in the 10.3 release notes. \\n\\n The way it works, though, is that unless we do something, nothing will show up in the release notes on this. \\n\\n We have a number of choices; \\n1. adjust\\/falsify history and change the comment for revision 453886 to belong to for instance   DERBY-1501  , or maybe   DERBY-1494  ... \\n2. close this bug as fixed in 10.3 and add the release note here. \\n\\n I vote for 2. \\n\\n I propose the following: \\n \\n\\t log a new bug (if not done already) for the issue with the type incompatibility of OUT parameters for stored procedures and link this new bug to   DERBY-310  . \\n\\t close this bug as fixed in 10.3. \\n\\t removing the existing application impact check from   DERBY-1501   because no change specific to that bug went into subversion, so a release note seems contrary. \\n \\n\\n\\n I understand your concern about giving the impression that all type differences were resolved, but then again, I don\'t think a release note about a fix is the appropriate place for that. So, I suggest we use verbage that suggests more differences may exist. \\n\\n I propose something like the following for the release note, please review &amp; correct: \\n------------------------------ \\nSummary of Change \\nDerby\'s Client implementation will return an appropriate error, matching the behavior with Embedded in the a number of situations related to PreparedStatement.setNull(int, int).  \\n\\n Symptoms Seen by Applications Affected by Change \\nIn a number of situations, Derby\'s client implementation behaved differently from the Embedded implementation: \\n1. setNull(LONGVARCHAR) on parameter of type CHAR FOR BIT DATA (Types.BINARY). \\n\\tIn previous releases, the Client succeeds, embedded fails (state 22005). \\n2. setNull(LONGVARBINARY) on parameter of type CHAR FOR BIT DATA (Types.BINARY). \\n\\tIn previous releases, Embedded succeeds, client fails (state 22005). \\n3. setNull(LONGVARBINARY) on parameter of type VARCHAR FOR BIT DATA (Types.VARBINARY). \\n\\tIn previous releases, Embedded succeeds, client fails (state 22005). \\n4. setNull(BINARY) on parameter of type LONG VARCHAR FOR BIT DATA (Types.LONGVARBINARY) \\n\\tIn previous releases, Embedded succeeds, client fails (state 22005). \\n5. setNull(TIME) on parameter of TIMESTAMP.  \\n\\tIn previous releases, Client succeeds, embedded fails (state 22005). \\n\\n\\n Incompatibilities with Previous Release \\nNow, in the cases indicated above, the client and Embedded implementation show the behavior previously shown only with Embedded. \\n\\n Rationale for Change \\nDerby\'s Client implementation and Embedded implementation should behave the same way from the point of view of an application whenever possible. \\n\\n Application Changes Required \\nApplications relying on the Client behaving in the old way will have to be adjusted. \\n------------------------------ \\n\\n If I do not hear objections, I\'ll proceed with this plan. \\n             \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n\u003c\\/div\u003e\\n                             \\n\\n\\n\u003cdiv
